Chapter Summaries

242/242 chapters summarised. Running kill count: ☠ 352

  • 001 1. Chapter 1

    A gamer from our world wakes up in Night City, 2075, in the body of fourteen-year-old Kusanagi Motoko — stripped of cyberware by Scavs, rescued, and coma-bound for a year. She can't walk, can't remember being Motoko, and the doctors couldn't care less. The Cyberpunk setting clicks into place fast, and with it the terror of knowing exactly how disposable a weak, unchipped kid is in this city.

    Hot-headed Tyger Claw enforcer Junichiro "Jun-Nii" Kusanagi storms into the hospital room with a katana on his hip and fire in his hair, swearing his little sister is safe. He brings her home to a cramped Japantown apartment reeking of old incense and burrito wrappers. Between awkward sibling bonding and wheelchair-bound leg raises, she starts piecing together the life of the girl she replaced — generational Tyger Claw family, dead parents, and a box of blood-stained clothes.

    Buried at the bottom of that box: a shard labelled "Gema / Gamer" in a pristine case. She slots it, blacks out, and wakes to find the Cyberpunk 2077 stat screen burning in her HUD — Body, Reflexes, Cool, Technical Ability, Intelligence, all scraping the floor. The first XP notification pops after a set of leg raises. By nightfall she discovers the system's instant-sleep recovery, and the rested XP buff glowing behind her eyelids seals it. The grind has begun.

    Date: 2022-10-15  |  AO3 ↗

  • 002 2. Chapter 2

    The Gamer System's instant-sleep recovery turns Motoko into a grinding machine. She burns through pushups, crunches, and stair climbs on a loop — exercise until collapse, sleep two hours, wake fully healed, repeat. Body hits Level 1 and suddenly she can stand without wobbling. Her first walk outside takes her around the block past Cherry Blossom Market, buying mystery meatballs from a street vendor while gunshots echo somewhere in the distance and nobody flinches.

    Jun drops a Unity handgun and a combat knife on the kitchen table with a one-hour crash course on not shooting herself. She spends every waking moment after that grinding draw-and-fire drills and knife work, unlocking both Handguns and Blades. The skills cap at Level 1 until Reflex catches up — a hard lesson in the system's stat-gating that leaves her grinding blade throws to push Reflex over the line.

    Her HUD has been a mess since the hospital — icons shifting with every eye twitch, menus flipping sides at random. A trip to the scarred Ripperdoc near Cherry Blossom Market reveals the embarrassing truth: she's been stuck in new-user setup mode since the Scavs stripped her chrome. With the HUD locked down and a gun holster plus knife sheath from the local shop strapped on, she walks home feeling armed, oriented, and — for the first time — like she belongs on these streets.

    Date: 2022-10-15  |  AO3 ↗

  • 003 3. Chapter 3

    Hiromi — Motoko's best friend, all-mohawk and no brakes, secret daughter of Arasaka execs — kicks the apartment door open and physically drags her to Ho-Oh, the Tyger Claw youth bar in Kabuki. There she meets the crew for the first time again: Ichi, the only one with a plan; Malcolm, who immediately tries to collect a fake debt. And Omaeda, the heavyset netrunner who barely looks up from his battered deck. Three hours of stories about the old Motoko paint a picture of a street-kid hellion she no longer recognizes.

    Drunk Hiromi tries to ride her Yaiba Kusanagi home. Motoko flat-out refuses to get on the back, wrestles the keys away, and drives the bike herself — badly, but alive. The system registers a new Driving skill under Reflex, which means non-game skills exist and the rules are wider than she thought. Back at the apartment, Hiromi lets slip that Motoko's late mother Natasha was a Tyger Claw netrunner, and that her Arasaka katana was almost certainly stripped by the Scavs.

    Two things stick after Hiromi passes out drooling on her shoulder. First: a conversation with some workers tips her off to a Scav nest at Megabuilding H2, Floor 24 — filed away for when she's strong enough to do something about it. Second: Blades hits Level 2 and the perk screen opens. She takes Ambidextrous, making both hands equally deadly. A knife in the left, a Unity in the right. Night City just got a little more dangerous.

    Date: 2022-10-15  |  AO3 ↗

  • 004 4. Chapter 4 ☠ 3

    Motoko hits Body Level 3 — the baseline of the game's protagonist V — and Jun takes her to the secret Tyger Claw underground shooting range beneath a compound in Little China. A grizzled range master watches her quick-draw and is impressed enough to hand over a Saratoga SMG for her to test. She burns through magazines unlocking Assault, pushing Handguns to Level 2, and taking the Quick Draw perk. She spends an hour teaching Jun the same draw technique — keeping her brother alive matters more than one session of XP.

    Hiromi drags everyone into a car-theft gig against Gonzales, a fake-Valentino drug pusher working the Kabuki shanty town. The plan falls apart fast: Omaeda can't crack the car's security, Malcolm's distraction act wears thin, and Hiromi gets pistol-whipped unconscious by one of Gonzales's guards. Ichi tries to bluff his way through the confrontation alone. When both guards raise their SMGs on him, Motoko creeps up behind all three, steals the chromed revolver off Gonzales's hip, and opens fire with both hands — Unity in the right, stolen revolver in the left.

    Both guards drop. Gonzales lunges at Ichi and catches a round for it. Three dead, Motoko coated in someone else's blood, and the whole crew staring at her like she might be the next thing they need to worry about. She loots the bodies on autopilot — two SMGs, eddie shards, ammo — then drives Hiromi's bike home in a dissociative haze while a Tyger Claw woman at the club washes the gore off her face. The soda she's given is sweet. The spilled puddle on the table is red. She pukes on Jun's shoes.

    ☠ 3 kills: dual-wields to drop Gonzales's two guards (one via revolver, one via Unity), then shoots Gonzales himself when he charges Ichi. First deliberate killings.

    Date: 2022-10-15  |  AO3 ↗

  • 005 5. Chapter 5

    Three bodies and a Cold Blood skill-up later, Motoko holes up in the apartment for days. The system gave her a full level-up for the kills — free stat point, free skill point — and the reward feels like poison. She won't leave, won't stop exercising, won't touch the Unity without her hands shaking. Jun eventually drags her out for ramen at Cherry Blossom Market. The city still has murder in it. But it also has noodles.

    Hiromi visits to say thanks — not for saving the gig, but for dropping the guys who cracked her skull. Her Arasaka-exec mother invites Motoko to dinner at the family's corpo apartment in Japantown, looks her over with clinical detachment, and approves: someone willing to kill for her daughter is an acceptable friend. Five thousand eddies hit Motoko's account without a word of explanation. Hiromi is furious. Motoko pockets it.

    Back at the shooting range her hands still shake on the draw. She pushes through it anyway, grinding Assault to Level 2 and taking the Gun Nut perk — pick up any weapon and instantly know its quirks, its failure points, its kill potential. The grizzled range master hands her Morgan Blackhand's *Solo's Manual*. Chapter Four lays out a philosophy on why a solo kills: defend yourself, protect your people, and flatline Scavs on sight. She reads it twice. Her hands slow their shaking.

    Date: 2022-10-17  |  AO3 ↗

  • 006 6. Chapter 6

    Athletics hits Level 1 and the Parkour perk rewires how she sees the city — every AC unit, window ledge, and overhang becomes a route. She takes the train to the corpo Chrome Ring Gym, a soulless glass-and-chrome palace in another district, and hammers weights until Body nears Level 5. The gym's punching machines catch her eye on the way out. One session later, Street Brawler is unlocked and she's got another skill tree to feed.

    She dyes her hair purple and cuts it short in the back, long in the front — the Major's look from Ghost in the Shell, because if you're going to steal a legend's name you might as well commit. Shopping with Hiromi yields a neo-military half-jacket and fingerless gloves. No Tyger Claw branding. Not now, not ever. Hiromi sulks about it.

    Ichi's crew picks up a low-stakes gig — babysitting a Tyger Claw debtor through an evening to make sure he doesn't flee town. She shows up armed to the teeth with an SMG, embarrasses herself, and watches through a boring stakeout that ends with a drunk guy stumbling into his apartment. The pay is pocket change split five ways. Riding home on the back of Hiromi's bike, she notices the quiet disappointment that nobody gave her a reason to pull the trigger. The addiction is growing teeth.

    Date: 2022-10-19  |  AO3 ↗

  • 007 7. Chapter 7

    Maelstrom borgs hit the Tyger Claw Casino at Longshore — retaliation for twelve dead Strom in a warehouse eviction two days prior. The Ho-Oh club shooting was a feint, something Motoko pieces together before anyone else. She's doing guard duty at Ho-Oh with Ichi when every Tyger Claw in the room gets the call simultaneously. Eyes glow, faces twist, and the bar empties in seconds. Shobo confirms it: the real hit is the casino.

    She races to Longshore on the back of Ichi's bike, nearly shoves a Unity under a guard's chin to get past the perimeter, and spends an agonizing stretch unable to reach Jun through the Maelstrom jammer. When comms finally cut back in, Jun picks up — alive, but shot in the shoulder. A close friend didn't make it. He hands her his bike key, tells her to go home, and disappears into the crowd of wounded and dead.

    She drives the Kusanagi home alone, Driving hitting Level 2 somewhere on the empty late-night streets. Back at the apartment she cleans everything — every dust bunny, every hidden burrito wrapper — because her hands need something to do that isn't reaching for a gun. Jun sends a single text the next afternoon: he's fine, he's with the Claws, no details. Then silence. She sits helpless, knowing her hothead brother is planning revenge and not yet strong enough to stop him.

    Date: 2022-10-20  |  AO3 ↗

  • 008 8. Chapter 8 ☠ 1

    Jun is still dark. Motoko trains Blades with Hiromi at the corpo apartment — Hiromi is better with a sword, faster, trained at an actual dojo, but she gasses out in three bouts while Motoko barely breathes hard. After that she spirals into a furious midnight parkour run, pushing Athletics to Level 5, vaulting through Maelstrom-adjacent streets with no destination and no plan.

    She finds one anyway. A borged-out Cyberpsycho cornering a couple in a back alley, ranting about thieves and territory. She rushes him with the knife. He catches her wrist with a chrome hand, shatters her ribs with a kick, and drops her. Unity rounds spark off his armored skull like firecrackers. But the Gamer System's 1-HP mechanic keeps her conscious through the broken bones — she grabs his own Burya revolver off the concrete and puts four heavy rounds through his chest. He dies standing up.

    She limps home with shattered ribs, sleeps eight hours, and wakes completely healed. Cool leveled up. Handguns leveled up. Cold Blood leveled up. She takes Cat-like and Cool Nerves as perks, cleans the battered Burya, and keeps it. Then she sits on the couch staring at the ceiling with her fingers tapping her knee, unable to ignore the truth knocking around her skull: she enjoyed it. The fight. The kill. The reward. Jun is still unreachable, and the siren call of the murder-XP loop is getting harder to resist.

    ☠ 1 kill: Maelstrom Cyberpsycho in an alley, stopped from murdering a couple. Shot with Psycho's own Burya revolver after Unity rounds bounced off chrome skull.

    Date: 2022-10-22  |  AO3 ↗

  • 009 9. Chapter 9

    With Jun still gone and the murder-XP itch clawing at her, Motoko walks to Jig-Jig Street and talks her way into Wakako Okada's pachinko-parlor office. The fixer doesn't bother learning her name — just drops a test gig: steal an info shard from a man holed up with Valentinos in a chop shop across town. No instructions on method. Wakako wants to see what kind of merc walks back through the beaded curtain.

    She parks Jun's bike blocks away and goes in over the rooftops. Parkour gets her onto the chop shop's roof; a security camera and a yard full of stolen cars block the back. While scouting for an entry she catches Dexter DeShawn pulling up and making a handoff with her target — she photographs the exchange. Ninjutsu hits Level 2 mid-infiltration, unlocking Danger Sense. She slips through an unlocked second-floor window, creeps downstairs, and chokes the target unconscious with a Grapple hold. No shots fired. She takes the shard, the target's laptop, and Dex's handoff item for good measure.

    Presenting the full haul to Wakako — info shard, laptop, Dex's mystery item, and the photo of the handoff — earns five thousand eddies and a spot on the fixer's contact list. First professional merc gig, clean non-lethal, with bonus intel on Dexter DeShawn thrown in for free. Walking out of the pachinko parlor she feels something she hasn't felt in days: productive. Useful. Like she belongs in this city on her own terms.

    Date: 2022-10-24  |  AO3 ↗

  • 010 10. Chapter 10

    Flush with Wakako's eddies, Motoko goes shopping for real. Combat boots from 6th Street territory, military-weave jeans, and the big ticket: a Militech Paraline Cyberdeck from Yoko at the Dewdrop Inn netrunner shop in Kabuki Market. It's old, it's cheap, and it's exactly what she needs. She takes it to the Japantown Ripperdoc and gets it installed with a custom neck port instead of the standard wrist cord — hands-free hacking, Major Kusanagi style.

    Back home she breaches everything in reach. Radio. TV. The burrito vending machine in the hallway — she seriously considers locking Jun out of it as punishment for going dark. Breach Protocol hits Level 2 and Quick Hacks unlocks via her mother's netrunning guide and a Ping program from Yoko. The apartment fills with cascading hack alerts as she pings every wireless device in range like a kid with a new toy.

    Jun finally walks through the door. Both arms are chrome now — cyberware from shoulder to fingertip, covered in fresh Tyger Claw tattoos, installed after the retribution raid on Maelstrom. He's quieter. Darker. Already talking about getting his legs done next. She warns him about cyberpsychosis; he shrugs it off. Hiromi reappears too, revealing her periodic vanishing acts are Arasaka Academy — her parents cut her comms if she doesn't attend. The tension breaks when Motoko teases Jun about his tattoos and his stupid swoop-seat bike until he dangles her upside down by one ankle and tickles her half to death.

    Date: 2022-10-26  |  AO3 ↗

  • 011 11. Chapter 11

    Motoko spends the morning grinding netrunning skills around Cherry Blossom Market, pinging vending machines and breaching camera networks until both Quick Hacks and Breach Protocol hit level 2. She picks up Wall Breaking and Cyber Security as her new perks -- backdoors into systems and hardened defenses against enemy netrunners. The real mission, though, is a trip to a hidden tailor shop down a dark Kabuki alley to pick up a custom order she has been planning for days.

    The shop sells netrunner suits behind a guarded back entrance, and the owner has cut one down to Motoko's specifications -- a modified leotard with armor weave, flexible enough for stealth work but tough enough to stop a bullet. A nod to the Major from Ghost in the Shell, and the first piece of gear that makes her feel like an actual edgerunner. Hiromi tags along, calls it weird corpo bodyguard chic, but Motoko does not care. She tosses the old T-shirt in the trash on the way out.

    Hiromi drags her to a Tyger Claw dance club dripping with faux-tatami floors and katana-wielding weebs. A rich kid named Tomaru tries to put his arm over Motoko's shoulder and gets a Unity pressed under his chin for the trouble. His crew bristles, Hiromi trades insults with him -- old school rivalry, apparently -- and a Tyger Claw enforcer steps in to break it up before blades come out. The night ends back on the dance floor, Motoko moving badly but moving all the same.

    Date: 2022-10-28  |  AO3 ↗

  • 012 12. Chapter 12

    Motoko reviews her stats and wrestles with the temptation to spend her hoarded stat and skill points. She pesters Wakako for work and gets a string of insultingly low-end gigs -- a courier run across the city via public transit, a bodyguard job for a woman retrieving a shard from an abusive boyfriend. The pay is practically nothing. Wakako is testing her patience, or maybe punishing her for being annoying.

    A ring ransom exchange in Rancho Coronado goes sideways when the teenage gang leader -- a kid with a shotgun and delusions of grandeur -- tries to rob her mid-deal. Motoko fires over one boy's head to scatter them, tackles the leader, pistol-whips his broken nose, and chucks her Unity at the gunman's skull when he lines up a second shot. She secures the ring, pays the full ransom anyway, and extracts the location of a 6th Street chop shop holding the client's stolen car. All while waiting for the bus home.

    Back at the apartment, the Maelstrom-Tyger Claw gang war is heating up and Jun has gone ghost -- two days without showing his face, responding only in clipped texts. The anxiety crystallizes into resolve. Motoko decides she needs to be strong enough to save Jun when the inevitable happens, and that means killing. She buys grenades, ammo, and a shoulder holster for the Burya from the gun shop. On the train ride out, she dumps both free stat points into Cool and both skill points into Ninjutsu -- Cool 4, Ninjutsu 4. She is going scav hunting.

    Date: 2022-10-30  |  AO3 ↗

  • 013 13. Chapter 13 ☠ 9

    Motoko infiltrates a scav den on Floor 24 of Megabuilding H2, dropping from the floor above and shimmying around an elevator shaft to bypass their camera network. The place reeks of blood, apartment walls smashed open to create a hive of ripper rooms and storage. She finds her first target scrolling a BD on the couch -- knife across the throat, pillow over the wound, move on.

    The stealth run claims four scavs by blade before a woman with reflex-boosted chrome dodges the first swipe and screams in Russian, blowing the operation open. Motoko throws her knife into the woman's chest and guns down a fifth scav scrambling for a Nokota D5 Copperhead. A borged-out enforcer with a tech shotgun pins her down, kicks back her first grenade, and blows a hole through the wall she was leaning on. She fakes him out with an unpinned grenade toss -- he moves to kick it and she puts a Burya round through his chrome at point blank, breaking her own arm in the process. Two more scavs go down in a desperate shootout that leaves Motoko bleeding out on the floor.

    A Max Doc keeps her alive long enough to finish the last scav with a bullet through the eye. She hauls herself onto the borg's couch to catch her breath amid crates full of harvested cyberware -- legs, arms, synth muscle, eyes. The loot is massive but she has no way to move it alone, so she calls Hiromi and Ichi's crew for cleanup. She showers off the blood, bandages the bullet holes under her jacket, and waits for her chooms to arrive with trucks.

    ☠ 9 kills: 4 scavs by knife (stealth), 1 woman (thrown knife), 1 by Copperhead rifle, 1 borged enforcer (Burya), 2 in the final shootout (Unity pistol).

    Date: 2022-11-01  |  AO3 ↗

  • 014 14. Chapter 14 ☠ 3

    Motoko is looting the borg's corpse when the elevator rumbles -- more scavs coming home. She sprints back through the den, drags the HMG from its bunker mount with her broken arm screaming, and sets up an ambush in the main room. Three scavs walk in, one carrying an unconscious victim over his shoulder. She opens fire from the hip and the HMG's explosive rounds turn the first man into hamburger, shred the second through his table cover, and send the third cowering behind a couch with the victim. Four Unity rounds finish him before he can look up.

    Hiromi and Ichi's crew arrive via the hijacked elevator to find a charnel house -- half-scavs on the floor, a borg with a hole through his chrome, and Motoko sitting calmly among the carnage with a broken arm and an HMG she refuses to leave behind. She casually recounts killing twelve scavs solo, which leaves her chooms staring in stunned silence. The crew loads five crates of harvested cyberware into Ichi's borrowed moving van and Malcolm's hatchback while Hiromi corners Motoko for an explanation.

    Hiromi is genuinely shaken -- this is edgerunner territory, not teenage merc work. Motoko admits she did it to get strong enough to protect Jun, who has been MIA in the gang war. The conversation is heavy but honest. The crew hauls the crates to Viktor Vektor's clinic in Watson, where Motoko gives away the entire haul in exchange for a relationship with a ripper she trusts. Vik chips Malcolm with a Militech smart link from the loot and sends them home. Motoko makes it back to an empty apartment, drops the HMG on the table, and realizes she forgot to check the scav garage for vehicles.

    ☠ 3 kills: 2 scavs obliterated by HMG explosive rounds, 1 executed with Unity pistol while shielding the victim.

    Date: 2022-11-03  |  AO3 ↗

  • 015 15. Chapter 15

    Motoko brokers the scav den's digital intel with Omaeda, letting the netrunner sell the data to his own contact in exchange for any scav location leads. Viktor goes through all five crates -- twenty-plus sets of limbs, an Arasaka show-piece arm, mid-range chrome across the board but nothing combat-rated. He finds a solid Militech smart link system and insists on paying Motoko ten thousand eddies despite her protests, calling even that amount a scam in her favor.

    The crew argues about Motoko giving the chrome away, but she splits Vik's payment evenly -- two grand each. Malcolm wins the smart link after a group huddle and gets chipped on the spot. Vik's clinic becomes Motoko's ripperdoc of choice, a relationship she values far above the eddies her chooms think she left on the table. Hiromi threatens to tell Jun; Motoko points out she would tell him herself if she ever saw him.

    Back at the apartment with her HMG, two thousand eddies, and a bag of scav weapons, Motoko takes stock. The Tyger Claw-Maelstrom war continues to swallow Jun whole. She hauls the machine gun inside, drops it on the living room table, and collapses on the couch -- only to bolt upright cursing when she realizes she never checked the scav den's parking garage for a getaway car.

    Date: 2022-11-05  |  AO3 ↗

  • 016 16. Chapter 16 ☠ 2

    Motoko grinds Intelligence by pinging every device on her jogging route, levels Street Brawler to 4 at the gym, and spends two days hacking vending machines and cameras across Kabuki. The monotony breaks when Wakako summons her to the parlor, where a Nomad named Scorpion -- Aldecaldos, real name Driss Meriana -- needs off-the-books security for a Raffen Shiv meet in the Badlands. He is buying a Brennan Apollo motorcycle from an ex-family member named Connor who fell in with the Wraiths. Two-three hundred eddies after haggling, and Motoko takes the gig.

    The four-hour drive out is quiet. Scorpion is impressed by the HMG in his back seat and the girl's military-grade composure. At the wayhouse, Motoko clears the perimeter, hacks a rooftop position, and practically vanishes against the AC unit. The exchange with Connor goes smooth -- bike for eddies, family letters for a kid who got expelled from the Aldecaldos. Then engines roar from the south. Five Wraith vehicles bearing down. Connor bolts, Scorpion fumbles with the trailer hitch, and Motoko unhooks it so they can run.

    She leans out the passenger window with her SMG and drops a biker, then straps the HMG to a seatbelt and fires it one-handed out the open door -- shredding a Wraith truck before a blown tire sends the Gecko flipping across the dunes. Motoko is thrown clear. She crawls back with a bullet hole through her shoulder, stabs the Raffen who charges her, and slits his throat before Frank -- the Wraith leader -- puts a rifle round through her chest. Scorpion watches her fall and whispers an apology as they drag him away.

    ☠ 2 kills: 1 Wraith biker (SMG from moving car), 1 Wraith fighter (stabbed and throat-slit after being thrown from the crash).

    Date: 2022-11-07  |  AO3 ↗

  • 017 17. Chapter 17 ☠ 10

    Motoko huffs a Max Doc in the sand, straps on a dead Wraith's goggles and dust mask, and starts walking. An interlude shows Ichi drinking at the Ho-oh Club, confessing jealousy to an older Tyger Claw named Hatake over Motoko's impossible solo feats. Hatake's advice is blunt -- edgerunners burn bright and die young, probably before sixteen at this rate. Meanwhile Motoko trudges an hour through the sandstorm to the wayhouse, finds the motorcycle trailer already gone, and ambushes Connor when he stumbles inside. Gun in his mouth, she extracts the Wraith compound's GPS coordinates and walks back into the storm alone.

    She dumps both free stat points into Cool 8 and Ninjutsu 7 before breaching the compound's camera network, uploading a daemon that blurs her from every Wraith's optics. Intelligence hits level 3 from the hack. Then she ghosts through the camp -- throat-slit the security monitor mid-noodles, screwdriver through Kengo's ear in the barracks, a carpenter's hammer into Boomer's skull at his workbench. Eight men die without a single alarm.

    Frank Elder -- the Wraith leader -- emerges from his basement to find a ghost town. Every room is a charnel house. He panics, fires blind with his Overture, and tries to auto-drive his Quadra Type-66 Reaver to the exit. Motoko is already in the passenger seat. A Burya round blows him out of his own car. She pulls his key shard from his neck port, pockets his Overture, and finishes him with it. Then she goes downstairs to cut Scorpion loose.

    ☠ 10 kills: 8 Wraiths by stealth (knife, screwdriver, hammer, and other improvised weapons), 1 Wraith (Burya to the chest in his own car), 1 Frank Elder (executed with his own Overture).

    Date: 2022-11-09  |  AO3 ↗

  • 018 18. Chapter 18

    Motoko cuts Scorpion down from the chains in Frank's basement, feeds him a Max Doc, and hauls him to the stolen Quadra Type-66 Reaver. She drives the beaten nomad to the Aldecaldos camp -- arriving in a Wraith-marked muscle car, which gets every rifle in camp pointed at her hood. Cassidy, a cowboy-hat-wearing nomad with a drawl, takes custody of Scorpion and offers their doc. Motoko declines, passes along the Wraith compound coordinates for looting, and drives off before anyone can ask too many questions.

    The long drive home levels her Driving skill to 3. She parks the Reaver in Jun's empty garage spot, showers off layers of blood and desert grit, and sleeps until her wounds heal. Wakako summons her for a debrief -- the fixer has already received Scorpion's detailed after-action report and Aldecaldos crime scene photos. A screwdriver in a dead man's ear has earned Wakako's genuine respect. The fixer promotes Motoko from disposable rookie to stealth specialist, promising dangerous but well-paying gigs if she can prove herself on infiltration work.

    Scorpion texts his thanks and confirms the Aldecaldos recovered his Brennan Apollo from the compound. Motoko eats ramen at Cherry Blossom Market, learns to sew from a market vendor to repair her bullet-riddled netrunner suit, and earns her first Crafting XP from stitching fabric. Wakako's interlude reveals the fixer had originally sent Motoko on the nomad gig as a lesson in saying no to bad jobs -- she never expected the girl to single-handedly wipe a Raffen Shiv camp and walk home in a stolen car.

    Date: 2022-11-12  |  AO3 ↗

  • 019 19. Chapter 19

    Motoko takes a few days off from killing to grind Crafting and Technical skills. She buys a thousand-eddie tool kit from a market repair lady, drives her Reaver back into the Badlands to recover her wrecked HMG from the desert sand, and discovers the gun took a fatal hit to its receiver during the crash. Crafting level 1 unlocks a dense knowledge dump -- deconstruction, explosives theory, tool handling, weapon repair -- and she hauls the dead HMG home as a future restoration project.

    A trip to the city dump for scrap electronics turns surreal when she stumbles across a familiar fridge half-buried in garbage. Inside: the decomposing corpse of Rache Bartmoss, the legendary netrunner who created the craft. She grabs his netdeck, dry-heaves her way back to the car, and seals it in a plastic bag. Too dangerous to crack open now -- she will need far higher Intelligence and netrunning skills before touching whatever is inside. She stashes it in her room and tells no one.

    The gang war dominates the news. Valentinos, 6th Street, and the Moxes have all been pulled into the Tyger Claw-Maelstrom conflict, turning the north side of Night City into a warzone. Jun is still completely silent. Hiromi finishes school and races over on her Kusanagi to interrogate Motoko about the Badlands job, gets the highlights -- HMG out a car door, Wraith camp, stolen ride -- and demands to see the Reaver. Motoko shows off her new wheels and the two head out for a drive.

    Date: 2022-11-15  |  AO3 ↗

  • 020 20. Chapter 20

    Motoko and Hiromi cruise the city in the Wraith-marked Reaver, stop by the Ho-oh Club to show off the car to Ichi. A text from Viktor Vektor hits different -- he has been installing the scav-den chrome on kids who lost limbs, sending pictures of children with new legs and prosthetic arms. Motoko tears up in the parking lot. Ichi shrugs it off, but Hiromi goes quiet looking through the photos, seeing a side of Motoko she did not expect.

    Vik has also tracked down a set of Kiroshi Mk1 optics for Motoko. She drives to his clinic with Hiromi riding shotgun as a self-appointed bodyguard. The installation goes smooth -- 720p vision jumps to 4k, scanner syncs near-instantly with her Quick Hack targeting, and a built-in lens disruptor blurs her face on any surveillance camera. She pays Vik full price despite the chrome debt, which makes Hiromi grind her teeth. Misty watches the Wraith car outside while they are in the basement.

    Driving home with new eyes, everything is sharper -- she can clock vehicle speeds at a glance, read pores on Hiromi's face from across the car. Driving skill ticks up to level 4. Hiromi teases her about having a crush on Vik, gets an unblinking Kiroshi death-stare in return, and wisely backs down. They head back to the apartment for food and a movie. The gang war grinds on outside, Jun remains unreachable, and Motoko's old Arasaka Rainbow optics sit in a thermos at Vik's clinic -- the last trace of whoever she was before the scavs took her apart.

  • 021 21. Chapter 21

    Motoko digs into her stat sheet after Hiromi heads home, discovering new system mechanics -- Adaptation for cyberware, a raised Technical Attribute cap from her Kiroshi optics, and two fresh perk slots. She picks Parry for Blades and Improvised Weapons for Street Brawler, the latter putting her one perk away from Gun-Fu. The real grind begins at her workbench, disassembling scrap electronics for Technical XP while stewing over Jun's maddening two-word text: "I'm alive."

    Days blur into a cycle of soldering, breaching, and building. She rebuilds laptops from scrap, fabricates a working fan she controls via quickhack, and levels Crafting enough to unlock a perk -- choosing Robotics Wizard on a hunch about a secret project. A jog through Watson becomes a revelation when she starts pinging every connected device in sight and realizes Intelligence isn't raw smarts but netrunning comprehension. She jacks into a local network node and enters the Net for the first time -- a dazzling void of light and data bridges stretching into darkness.

    The brief dive nearly fries her Militech Paraline cyberdeck, leaving the hardware scalding hot against the back of her skull. She staggers down to a hacked vending machine, presses a cold can to her overheating port, and quotes Ghost in the Shell to the Night City sky. Quickhacking hits level 3, Intelligence surges toward 5, and Breach Protocol ticks up to 3 -- all from one reckless toe-dip into cyberspace. Back home she returns to her wire work, shocked awake later that night by gunfire outside the apartment.

With nothing but her Unity pistol, bare feet, and a three-story drop between her and the fight, she picks her target -- a Borg carrying a Carnage shotgun.

The next day brings Body 6, Annihilation 4, and a Driving level-up from the truck crash.   • 025 25. Chapter 25 ☠ 1

"I didn't ask for this," she whispers, channeling Adam Jensen before stuffing it down.

Her Breach Protocol and Intelligence both leveled during the hack. She escaped through a window with the laptop.

    The third gig was a corpo apartment heist for a fancy statue. The target's skyscraper had LMG turrets and cameras in the lobby—all running on radioshack-grade security that Motoko breached in seconds. She rode the elevator to the eighth floor, crept through the apartment while the owner entertained a joytoy, hid in a walk-in closet during an unfortunate ten minutes, then grabbed the statue from the bar on her way out. The first prototype was so bad she wanted to mercy-kill it on sight. She scaled back to individual limb design, thinking smaller—Flathead-sized units, eventually AI-driven. The AI problem loomed large; even Delamain needed a room-sized core, and she was designing something knee-height. Engineering alerts pinged steadily as she iterated through failures.

    Jun interrupted the design session with an invitation—another Kamikaze raid, and this time she could come. Motoko almost refused; she wanted to keep designing robots. But the XP called, and she had her Nekomata to level. She grabbed the sniper rifle with sudden eagerness, already picturing wall-bang kills while the Kamikaze played battering ram. Jun looked pleased, thinking he'd kept his sister at safe distance. He had no idea she planned to shoot through every wall between her and the Maelstrom.

  • 074 74. Chapter 74

    Motoko wakes in the basement with blood caked into her netrunner suit, cleans up, and checks the damage report from the corrupted server dive. She dumps five skill points and a stat point in rapid succession: Programming rockets from 5 to 10, Intelligence hits 10. She sways on her feet, Jun catches her, and she collapses onto the couch under a blanket.

    When the fog clears, the knowledge is transformative. She can see every flaw in her old code. She understands rudimentary AI construction. She selects two perks -- Inspired Programmer, which keeps creative momentum flowing endlessly, and A.I. Whisperer, which opens the door to creating true digital life. Jun hovers, worried about the near-collapse, but Motoko shrugs it off and opens her laptop. Programming 10 means she can rewrite everything from scratch -- and she intends to.

  • 075 75. Chapter 75

    Motoko opens the source code for Ping and recoils. At Programming 10 the bloated mess reads like an insult. She scraps it entirely and rebuilds from scratch -- a stealthy, compact program that slips through systems without ringing the bell. Where the original blasted every connected device with requests, Ping 2.0 uses Ghost Touch principles to silently trace network connections. Jun has to physically close her laptop to make her eat; she's been coding all day without noticing the sun set.

    Hiromi crashes the apartment on Jun's orders to snap Motoko out of her coding fugue. She drives the blade through Kanada's heart and spine in one thrust, rides the momentum to shove his body straight through the plate-glass window, then holds the dripping katana while locking eyes with Moritaka Kuwabara. A perfect Chiburi blood-shake, a cold delivery of 'Hayato Nakagawa sends her regards,' and she steps out through the shattered window onto Ichi's waiting truck.

Motoko brushes off the concern, insisting the music gig is the side hustle.

    After the party, the Kusanagi siblings argue their way home -- Jun livid about being blindsided, Motoko insistent she just forgot. She changes out of the kimono, racks her three Katana (Thermal, Musashi, and the new Kensei blade), and heads to the MSM recording studio the next day where the real fight begins: a producer who can't stop adding reverb to every note, bandmates who want to let the professionals work, and Motoko refusing to let anyone butcher her songs.

    Date: 2025-11-20  |  AO3 ↗

  • 237 237. Chapter 237

    Motoko survives a photo shoot with a domineering photographer who critiques her unpolished chrome, then gets ambushed by Alex Angelopoulos -- MSM's slick new "assistant" assigned to manage her. He's a corporate handler disguised as a helpful liaison, dangling restaurant reservations, celebrity meet-ups, and Militech Eagle cyberarms in front of her like bait. The Eagle specs are genuinely tempting -- Orbital Crystal reinforcement, double the dexterity of her Condors, modular weapon mounts -- but Motoko sees the devil's bargain underneath and tells him to talk to Hiromi.

    Back at the apartment, Jun listens to her vent about MSM's corporate playbook -- the assistant trick designed to wedge between artist and manager. The conversation derails when Jun gleefully recounts how young Motoko once dug a used Cybermatrix Holo Tattoo out of the trash behind Ryder's clinic and got it chipped in. The chrome had been pulled from a rotting corpse. Motoko's horror is palpable.

    A late-night call from Wakako snaps her back to business: a TC wife-killer needs his murder weapon pulled from a hidden safe before the NCPD finds it. Motoko races to the apartment only to find cops already inside -- the dead woman had police connections, explaining the fast response. She hacks the TV to blast Watson Whore at max volume as a distraction, slips through a bedroom window, cracks the safe (which beeps loud enough to alert every badge in the building), and Sandy-dashes out with the Unity pistol just ahead of the officers.

    Date: 2026-02-04  |  AO3 ↗

  • 238 238. Chapter 238

    Motoko collects from Wakako after the messy gun retrieval -- the fixer admits the dead woman was likely an undercover cop, explaining the rapid NCPD response. Frustrated by the Rockerboy grind, Motoko hits a Japantown gun range with her Tactician Shotgun to grind Annihilation, burning through shells in a meditative loop of fire-pump-reload until the skill XP ticks over toward level 6.

    MSM throws a rooftop launch party for Stand Alone Complex's debut single Pretender, rubbing shoulders with Night City's rich and famous. Motoko orders Beef Wellington, real baked potato, and a sushi platter on MSM's tab -- then nearly stabs Alex's hand to the table when he reaches for her food. The band plays Pretender to a room of indifferent elites, and Motoko pours genuine fury into every lyric because the performance interrupted her meal.

    After the set, Kitty Thunder -- the star of Watson Whore, playing drunk but razor-sharp underneath -- cozies up to the band and whispers a pointed warning about Alex into Motoko's ear during a photo op. Alex pushes hard to get Motoko on Kitty's show and into more brand deals, but Motoko deflects everything to Hiromi. The ride home in MSM's limo cements her suspicion: Alex isn't just annoying, he's dangerous enough that even a seasoned actress felt the need to flag it.

    Date: 2026-02-09  |  AO3 ↗

  • 239 239. Chapter 239 ☠ 5

    Motoko and Hiromi hash out the MSM situation over noodles -- Alex keeps setting up gigs behind Hiromi's back, forcing her to rubber-stamp deals or cost MSM money. They agree to let him dig his own grave while Hiromi learns his corporate playbook, with murder firmly on the table the moment he crosses the line. At the recording studio, another night of fighting with the sound tech over electronic edits to Everlong leaves Motoko boiling, and she tears out of the MSM parking garage on the Kusanagi looking for trouble.

    Trouble finds her at a Valentino-run rooftop pit fight in an emptied swimming pool. A chrome-skulled 6th Street banger called the American Devil has been dominating all comers, and when he chucks a half-full beer cup into Motoko's face, she drops into the pool fists-first. The brawl is brutal -- he's a better boxer with an armored brain case and chrome fists -- but Motoko wall-runs the pool, launches off some poor gonk's crotch, and lands an aerial haymaker that folds the Devil cold. She kicks him in the nuts for good measure.

    When 6th Street draws guns over their champion's loss, Motoko hits them with a Mass Weapon Glitch and goes feral. Her own song blasts from the radio as she donkey-kicks the first ganger off the rooftop, pulls her knife, and carves through the rest. She rides one screaming 6th Streeter off the edge of the building like a surfboard. Back home, she tells Jun she's never felt better -- sometimes a girl just needs a little extreme hyperviolence.

    ☠ 5 kills: one 6th Street ganger kicked off the rooftop, one surfed off the building edge, and three more cut down with knife and stolen gun after their weapons were glitched offline.

    Date: 2026-03-18  |  AO3 ↗

  • 240 240. Chapter 240

    Motoko wakes up feeling nova after the rooftop bloodbath, reviews her Street Brawler XP gains, and heads to Lizzie's Bar to drop off the fight BD with Judy Alvarez. She finds the editor running on energy drinks alongside Evelyn Parker -- the blue-haired Clouds doll who'll one day kick off the Konpeki heist. Evelyn excuses herself when Motoko arrives, and Judy grudgingly accepts the shard after confirming there are no eyeballs in this one.

    Lunch with Malcolm and Ichi at the Sakura Market ramen stall turns into therapy when Malcolm tells Motoko to stop hyperfocusing on the negatives of her MSM deal and start milking the perks -- real food, rich contacts who need mercs, free chrome. Ichi confesses he's been using the Minotaur mech enough to seize its ankle actuator, nearly getting himself strangled before Malcolm's earnest intervention saves his life. The conversation reframes Motoko's Rockerboy frustrations as normal job complaints.

    Judy's POV closes the chapter as she edits Motoko's rooftop BD -- experiencing the pit fight through Motoko's emotional feed and marveling at the flat, iron confidence where fear should be. The Sandy-assisted wall-run punch lands with perfect clarity, and then the 6th Street massacre plays out in rapid succession: knife to jugular, stolen gun, and the stomach-dropping freefall of surfing a screaming ganger off a building. Judy pauses the scroll at impact and whispers a quiet curse.

    Date: 2026-03-19  |  AO3 ↗

  • 241 241. Chapter 241

    Motoko decides to embrace the perks of her Rockerboy life -- starting with the four bottles of expensive shampoo MSM's stylists gave her -- and heads to Vik's clinic for the Militech Eagle cyberarm installation. Outside Misty's Esoterica, she runs into Thomas Anderson, the Militech operative who once stabbed her and threw her out a twelfth-story window. He's now bodyguarding Katalina, the Militech middle manager overseeing the brand deal, and the two lock eyes in a mutual threat assessment before agreeing they aren't worth drawing on today.

    Katalina nearly torpedoes the entire event when she spots Hiromi's Arasaka Academy uniform and refuses to work with an enemy corpo's student. Alex swoops in to exploit the chaos -- his plan all along was to get Hiromi removed. Hiromi fires back with Militech's own loss projections, cornering Katalina with the math on what walking away would cost her quarterly report. The corpo folds, and the two women pivot into grudging mutual respect, bonding over cost-benefit analysis while Motoko worries about "Dommy Mommy wiles."

    Vik inspects the brand-new Militech Eagle Mk.V arms in his basement clinic -- Orbital Crystal reinforcement, thickened myomer, Gorilla arm mod, subdermal grip, and EMP-hardened shielding. A Militech doctor fusses about the warranty while Vik calmly strips panels to check for spyware. Cameras roll everywhere for the commercial shoot, and Motoko trades barbs with Thomas between takes, offering him a job with Section 9 (he declines) and promising to kill him next time they meet.

    Date: 2026-03-20  |  AO3 ↗

  • 242 242. Chapter 242

    Motoko wakes up on Vik's operating chair with brand-new Militech Eagle Mk.V arms -- silver chrome, sleeker than the old Condors, and packing enough myomer torque to rip doors off hinges. She refuses to say the cringey Militech taglines the corpo handler keeps feeding her, settling on "they feel like I can take on the world -- or at least a small corp" before the cameras finally stop rolling. The Eagles only require four adaptation points instead of five, refunding a stat point she immediately dumps into Sandevistan adaptation.

    Hiromi arrives glowing after outmaneuvering Alex's latest scheme and trades intel with Motoko about the MSM handler's ongoing attempts to undercut her authority. They agree he's still more annoyance than threat, but Hiromi quietly feeds Alex information about Motoko's merc work -- some kind of play Motoko can't quite read yet. Back at the apartment, Jun inspects the new arms with characteristic understatement and insists Motoko get them checked for bugs, not realizing Vik already swept them.

    The next morning, Vik runs Motoko through boxing drills in the alley outside his clinic -- jabs, weaves, and full Gorilla mod punches that rock the old fighter back on his heels. Street Brawler hits level 9 mid-session. Jun kicks her out of the apartment until five for a mysterious "business meeting," and every friend she calls is suspiciously unavailable. She walks through the door at five-oh-five to a room full of people screaming "Surprise!" -- and instinctively punches through the ceiling with one hand while drawing her Burya with the other. Happy birthday, Motoko.

    Date: 2026-03-22  |  AO3 ↗
